This post is a continuation of *[One λ-calculus, many times...](
{% post_url 2016-03-20-one-lambda-calculus-many-times %})*, in which I
explored the use natural deduction and sequent calculus systems as
type systems for the simply-typed lambda calculus.[^minproplog] In
this post, I will have a look at a variant of one of these systems
which has explicit structural rules: Gentzen's LJ.

<div class="hidden">
<pre class="Agda"><a name="666" class="Keyword">import</a><a name="672"> </a><a name="673" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#1" class="Module">2016-03-20-one-lambda-calculus-many-times</a><a name="714"> </a><a name="715" class="Symbol">as</a><a name="717"> </a><a name="718" class="Module">Part1</a><a name="723">
</a><a name="724" class="Keyword">module</a><a name="730"> </a><a name="731" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#1" class="Module" target="_blank">one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2</a><a name="763"> </a><a name="764" class="Keyword">where</a></pre>
</div>

The structure of this post will be very similar to that of part
one---which means that we will start out by having a look at the
syntax of NJ, and then have a look at its semantics and relation to
the system ND we discussed last time. But first, the syntax:

<pre class="Agda"><a name="1061" class="Keyword">module</a><a name="1067"> </a><a name="1068" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#1068" class="Module" target="_blank">Syntax</a><a name="1074"> </a><a name="1075" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="1076" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#1076" class="Bound" target="_blank">Atom</a><a name="1080"> </a><a name="1081" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="1082"> </a><a name="1083" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a><a name="1086" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="1087"> </a><a name="1088" class="Keyword">where</a></pre>

We can reuse our notions of types and sequents from the previous post:

<pre class="Agda Spec">  <a name="2644" class="Keyword">data</a><a name="2648"> </a><a name="2649" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#2649" class="Datatype">Type</a><a name="2653"> </a><a name="2654" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="2655"> </a><a name="2656" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a><a name="2659"> </a><a name="2660" class="Keyword">where</a><a name="2665">

  </a><a name="3950" class="Keyword">data</a><a name="3954"> </a><a name="3955" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#3955" class="Datatype">Sequent</a><a name="3962"> </a><a name="3963" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="3964"> </a><a name="3965" class="PrimitiveType">Set</a><a name="3968"> </a><a name="3969" class="Keyword">where</a><a name="3974">
    </a><a name="3979" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#3979" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">_⊢_</a><a name="3982"> </a><a name="3983" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="3984"> </a><a name="3985" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#52" class="Datatype" target="_blank">List</a><a name="3989"> </a><a name="3990" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#2649" class="Datatype">Type</a><a name="3994"> </a><a name="3995" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="3996"> </a><a name="3997" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#2649" class="Datatype">Type</a><a name="4001"> </a><a name="4002" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="4003"> </a><a name="4004" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#3955" class="Datatype">Sequent</a></pre>

Now, the usual axiomatisation for NJ is as follows:

$$
  \begin{array}{c}
  \frac{}{A \vdash A}{\small ax}
  \quad
  \frac{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\Gamma \vdash A \Rightarrow B}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!i}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash A \Rightarrow B \quad \Delta \vdash A}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!e}
  \\
  \\
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash B}{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\small w}
  \quad
  \frac{A , A , \Gamma \vdash B}{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\small c}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma , A , B , \Delta \vdash C}{\Gamma , B , A , \Delta \vdash C}{\small p}
  \end{array}
$$

<br />
There are three notable changes when comparing this to the system SC:

  - **Weakening**. The axiom no longer allows for arbitrary contexts
    to be present, it *has* to be $$A \vdash A$$. An implication of
    this is that we no longer have the option to have *unused*
    formulas in our context. If we *do* want to have unused formulas,
    we can add this using the *weakening* rule (or $$w$$).

  - **Contraction**. When we apply a binary rule, we no longer pass
    the entire context to both sides---instead, we have to choose
    how to *split* the context. So what do we do if there is a formula
    which we want to use in *both* branches of the proof? We can use
    the *contraction*[^contraction] (or $$c$$) rule, which *copies* a
    formula, and then pass a copy to either branch.

  - **Permutation**. The third change lies with the structure of our
    contexts and with the $$ax$$ rule. In the previous system, we
    thought of our contexts as *sets*, even though we implemented them
    with lists. This showed itself in the definition of the $$ax$$
    rule, which took an extra argument---a proof that the desired
    type $$A$$ was a member of the context $$\Gamma$$:

    $$
      \frac{A \in \Gamma}{\Gamma \vdash A}{\small ax}
    $$

    Without this, we've also lost the ability to have variables point
    to arbitrary positions in the context. In other words, our system
    is *ordered*. To remedy this, we've added add a third new rule:
    permutation (or $$p$$).

Below, I've implemented the resulting system in Agda:

href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#7041" class="Bound" target="_blank">C</a></pre>



### Admissible Structural Rules in ND

If we are to have any hope of proving the equivalence between the
implicit and the explicit systems, we should be able to prove that the
implicit systems admit[^admit] the same structural rules. In the
previous post, we've already proven the following theorem for ND:

> If $$\Gamma \subseteq \Gamma\prime$$ and $$\Gamma \vdash A$$, then
> $$\Gamma\prime \vdash A$$.

<div class="hidden">
<pre class="Agda">  <a name="7563" class="Keyword">module</a><a name="7569"> </a><a name="7570" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#7570" class="Module" target="_blank">ND</a><a name="7572"> </a><a name="7573" class="Keyword">where</a><a name="7578">
    </a><a name="7583" class="Keyword">open</a><a name="7587"> </a><a name="7588" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#1219" class="Module">Part1.</a><a name="7594" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#1566" class="Module">Syntax</a><a name="7600"> </a><a name="7601" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#1076" class="Bound" target="_blank">Atom</a><a name="7605"> </a><a name="7606" class="Keyword">public</a><a name="7612"> </a><a name="7613" class="Keyword">using</a><a name="7618"> </a><a name="7619" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="7620">w′</a><a name="7622" class="Symbol">)</a></pre>
</div>

And we've also shown that we can very easily use this theorem to
define weakening, because <a class="Agda InductiveConstructor Spec" target="_blank"
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227">there</a>
is a proof that "weakening", i.e.
<span class="Agda Spec"><a class="Bound">Γ</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#3056" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">⊆</a> <a class="Bound">A</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a> <a class="Bound">Γ</a></span>,
holds for the subset relationship.

<pre class="Agda Spec">    <a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#8603" class="Function">w′</a><a> </a><a class="Symbol">:</a><a> </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#5371" class="Datatype Operator">ND</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">Γ</a><a> </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#3979" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">⊢</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">B</a><a> </a><a class="Symbol">→</a><a> </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#5371" class="Datatype Operator">ND</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">A</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">Γ</a><a> </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#3979" class="InductiveConstructor Operator">⊢</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">B</a><a>
    </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#8603" class="Function">w′</a><a> </a><a class="Symbol">=</a><a> </a><a href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#7305" class="Function">struct</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a></pre>

Therefore, all we need to show to extend this to contraction and
permutation is that their respective equations,
<span class="Agda Spec"><a class="Bound">A</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a> <a class="Bound">A</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a> <a class="Bound">Γ</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#3056" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">⊆</a> <a class="Bound">A</a> <a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a> <a class="Bound">Γ</a></span>
and
<span class="Agda Spec"><a class="Bound">Γ</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Base.html#895" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">++</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">A</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">B</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">Δ</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#3056" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">⊆</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">Γ</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Base.html#895" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">++</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">B</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">A</a><a> </a><a href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a> </a><a class="Bound">Δ</a></span>,
hold for the subset relation as well.
This is simply a matter of reindexing.
For contraction, if our "index" (made up of
<a class="Agda Spec InductiveConstructor" target="_blank"
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1174">here</a>
and
<a class="Agda InductiveConstructor Spec" target="_blank"
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227">there</a>)
points to the first formula, we keep it the same. Otherwise, we
subtract one. That way, the first two formulas are *contracted*, and
the rest is adjusted accordingly.

<pre class="Agda">    <a name="12031" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12031" class="Function" target="_blank">c′</a><a name="12033"> </a><a name="12034" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="12035"> </a><a name="12036" class="Symbol">∀</a><a name="12037"> </a><a name="12038" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="12039" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12039" class="Bound" target="_blank">A</a><a name="12040"> </a><a name="12041" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12041" class="Bound" target="_blank">B</a><a name="12042"> </a><a name="12043" And for permutation, we skip through our index until we've passed the
$$\Gamma$$ portion of the context, and then we swap the first two
formulas.

        </a><a name="12680" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12544" class="Function" target="_blank">permute′</a><a name="12688"> </a><a name="12689" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#89" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">[]</a><a name="12691">      </a><a name="12697" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12698" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="12703"> </a><a name="12704" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12705" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1174" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">here</a><a name="12709"> </a><a name="12710" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12710" class="Bound" target="_blank">px</a><a name="12712" class="Symbol">))</a><a name="12714"> </a><a name="12715" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="12716"> </a><a name="12717" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1174" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">here</a><a name="12721"> </a><a name="12722" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12710" class="Bound" target="_blank">px</a><a name="12724">

        </a><a name="12794" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12544" class="Function" target="_blank">permute′</a><a name="12802"> </a><a name="12803" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12804" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12804" class="Bound" target="_blank">C</a><a name="12805"> </a><a name="12806" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a name="12807"> </a><a name="12808" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12808" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="12809" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="12810"> </a><a name="12811" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12812" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1174" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">here</a><a name="12816"> </a><a name="12817" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12817" class="Bound" target="_blank">px</a><a name="12819" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="12820">         </a><a name="12829" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="12830"> </a><a name="12831" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1174" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">here</a><a name="12835"> </a><a name="12836" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12817" class="Bound" target="_blank">px</a><a name="12838">
        </a><a name="12847" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12544" class="Function" target="_blank">permute′</a><a name="12855"> </a><a name="12856" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12857" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12857" class="Bound" target="_blank">C</a><a name="12858"> </a><a name="12859" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a name="12860"> </a><a name="12861" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12861" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="12862" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="12863"> </a><a name="12864" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12865" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="12870"> </a><a name="12871" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12871" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="12872" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="12873">         </a><a name="12882" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="12883"> </a><a name="12884" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="12889"> </a><a name="12890" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="12891" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12544" class="Function" target="_blank">permute′</a><a name="12899"> </a><a name="12900" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12861" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="12901"> </a><a name="12902" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#12871" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="12903" class="Symbol">)</a></pre>

So, do we have enough to prove equivalence between the two systems?
No, sadly we do not. If we have a look at the two versions of
$$\small{\Rightarrow}\!e$$, we see that they use contexts quite
differently...

$$
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash A \Rightarrow B \quad \Gamma \vdash A}{\Gamma \vdash B}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!e}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash A \Rightarrow B \quad \Delta \vdash A}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!e}
$$

If we were to try and use the second version to simulate the
first, we'd find that we end up with *two* copies of the context
$$\Gamma$$. We would need some souped up version of contraction to
contract these two contexts back into one... If, on the other hand, we
were to try and use the first version to simulate the second, we run
into a different problem: the first version of
$$\small{\Rightarrow}\!e$$ expects both premises to *share* a
context, but the premises have contexts $$\Gamma$$ and $$\Delta$$,
respectively. So we need two versions of weakening which can add an
entire *context* to the right or left, respectively.

$$
  \frac{\Gamma , \Gamma \vdash B}{\Gamma \vdash B}{\small c^+}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash B}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small inl}
  \quad
  \frac{\Delta \vdash B}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small inr}
$$

At this point, it may be a better idea to just derive a new, more
permissive set of structural rules. This is what we'll do in the next
section.

### More Expressive Structural Rules

The usual structural rules for NJ are theoretically sufficient, but in
practice they are rather limiting. Therefore, in this section, we will
present more permissive variants, and show that they too are
admissible in ND. Below you will see the more expressive variants of
the structural rules. Instead of weakening, contracting or permuting
formulas, these rules permute entire contexts.

I've added one new rule, $$\small f^+$$ or "forward". It's in
parenthesis because it is an obvious instance of permutation.
I've nontheless added it, though, because it will turn out to be a
useful lemma on the way to proving permutation.

$$
  \frac{\Delta \vdash B}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small w^+}
  \quad
  \left(
  \frac{\Gamma , \Sigma , A , \Delta \vdash C}{\Gamma , A , \Sigma , \Delta \vdash C}{\small f^+}
  \right)
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma , \Sigma , \Pi , \Delta \vdash C}{\Gamma , \Pi , \Sigma , \Delta \vdash C}{\small p^+}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma , \Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\Gamma , \Delta \vdash B}{\small c^+}
$$

Since we already have a structural theorem (<a
href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#7305" class="Agda
Spec Function">struct</a>) for ND, we only have to show that these
equations hold for the subset relationship.

Weakening is still quite trivial. Instead of applying <a class="Agda
InductiveConstructor Spec" target="_blank"
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227">there</a>
once, we now apply it multiple times, until we've removed the entire
context $$\Gamma$$.

<pre class="Agda">    <a name="15921" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15921" class="Function" target="_blank">weaken</a><a name="15927"> </a><a name="15928" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="15929"> </a><a name="15930" class="Symbol">∀</a><a name="15931"> </a><a name="15932" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15932" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="15933"> </a><a name="15934" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="15935"> </a><a name="15936" class="Symbol">∀</a><a name="15937"> </a><a name="15938" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="15939" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15939" class="Bound" target="_blank">Δ</a><a name="15940" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="15941"> </a><a name="15942" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="15943"> </a><a name="15944" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15939" class="Bound" target="_blank">Δ</a><a name="15945"> </a><a name="15946" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#3056" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">⊆</a><a name="15947"> </a><a name="15948" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15932" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="15949"> </a><a name="15950" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Base.html#895" class="Function Operator" target="_blank">++</a><a name="15952"> </a><a name="15953" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15939" class="Bound" target="_blank">Δ</a><a name="15954">
    </a><a name="15959" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15921" class="Function" target="_blank">weaken</a><a name="15965"> </a><a name="15966" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#89" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">[]</a><a name="15968">      </a><a name="15974" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15974" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="15975"> </a><a name="15976" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="15977"> </a><a name="15978" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15974" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="15979">
    </a><a name="15984" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15921" class="Function" target="_blank">weaken</a><a name="15990"> </a><a name="15991" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="15992" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15992" class="Bound" target="_blank">A</a><a name="15993"> </a><a name="15994" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#104" class="InductiveConstructor Operator" target="_blank">∷</a><a name="15995"> </a><a name="15996" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15996" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="15997" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="15998"> </a><a name="15999" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15999" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="16000"> </a><a name="16001" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="16002"> </a><a name="16003" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="16008"> </a><a name="16009" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="16010" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15921" class="Function" target="_blank">weaken</a><a name="16016"> </a><a name="16017" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15996" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="16018"> </a><a name="16019" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#15999" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="16020" class="Symbol">)</a></pre>

Forwards movement, or $$\small f^+$$, is a little bit more involved.
In <a class="Agda Spec Function">forward</a>, we skip the entire
context $$\Gamma$$. If the index points to some formula *in*
$$\Gamma$$, we don't have to do anything. Once we pass $$\Gamma$$, we
enter the nested function  <a class="Agda Spec Function">forward′</a>,
in which we recursively move the formula $$A$$ forward, step by step,
across the context $$\Sigma$$.

<pre class="Agda">    <a name="16489" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#16489" class="Function" target="_blank">forward</a><a name="16496"> </a><a class="Symbol">=</a><a name="16636"> </a><a name="16637" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="16642"> </a><a </a><a name="16652" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#16620" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="16653"> </a><a name="16654" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#16623" class="Bound" target="_blank">Σ</a><a name="16655"> </a><a name="16656" class="Symbol">|</a><a name="17019"> </a><a name="17020" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="17025"> </a><a name="17029"> </a><a name="17030" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="17035"> </a><a name="17036" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="17037" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Any.html#1227" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">there</a><a name="17042"> </a><a name="17043" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#17026" class="Bound" target="_blank">j</a><a name="17044" class="Symbol">)</a></pre>

With a rule for forwards movement in hand, we can start to prove
permutation. The proof itself is broken down in *two* cases: $$\Pi =
\emptyset$$ and $$\Pi = A , \Pi'$$.

$$
    \frac
    {\Gamma , \Sigma , \emptyset , \Delta \vdash C}
    {\Gamma , \emptyset , \Sigma , \Delta \vdash C}
    \quad
    \frac
    {\Gamma , \Sigma , A , \Pi' , \Delta \vdash C}
    {\Gamma , A , \Pi' , \Sigma , \Delta \vdash C}
$$

The first case is trivial, and simply requires rewriting by proofs of
right identity and associativity (as the actual sequent is
$$((\Gamma,\Sigma), (\emptyset,\Delta))$$). For the second case, we
prove the statement by moving the $$A$$ forwards across the $$\Sigma$$
(using $$\small f^+$$) and then permuting $$\Sigma$$ and $$\Pi'$$.
The proof in Agda, however, is rather hard to read. This is because
there is no pleasant way to intersperse code and rewrites (à la <a
class="Agda Spec Keyword">rewrite</a>). To help you decipher the
proof, I've inserted the intermediate terms as comments.

<pre class="Agda">    <a name="18082" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#18082" class="Function" target="_blank">permute</a><a name="18089"> </a><a       </a><a name="18223" class="Keyword">rewrite</a><a name="18230"> </a><a name="18231" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#1963" class="Function" target="_blank">++-identityʳ</a><a name="18243"> </a><a name="18244" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#18166" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="18245">

            </a><a name="18349" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="18350"> </a><a name="18351" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#18177" class="Bound" target="_blank">i</a><a name="18352">

           </a><a name="18395" class="Comment">-- x ∈ (Γ ++ A ∷ Σ) ++ Π ++ Δ</a><a name="18424">

    </a><a name="19674" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19580" class="Function" target="_blank">s⁺′</a><a name="19677"> </a><a name="19678" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="19679" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19679" class="Bound" target="_blank">A</a><a name="19680" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="19681"> </a><a name="19682" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19682" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="19683"> </a><a name="19684" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19684" class="Bound" target="_blank">Σ</a><a name="19685"> </a><a name="19686" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="19687" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19687" class="Bound" target="_blank">Π</a><a name="19688" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="19689"> </a><a name="19690" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19690" class="Bound" target="_blank">f</a><a name="19691">
      </a><a name="19698" class="Symbol">=</a><a name="19699"> </a><a name="19700" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Relation.Binary.PropositionalEquality.Core.html#705" class="Function" ### Deriving Structural Rules in NJ

<div class="hidden">
<pre class="Agda">  <a name="19945" class="Keyword">module</a><a name="19951"> </a><a name="19952" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#19952" class="Module" target="_blank">NJ</a><a name="19954"> </a><a name="19955" class="Keyword">where</a></pre>
</div>

We can derive these same extended structural rules in NJ. For
instance, below we derive the equivalent weakening rule:

<pre class="Agda">    <a name="20117" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20117" class="Function" target="_blank">w⁺′</a><a name="20120"> </a><a name="20121" The remainder of the proofs are rather similar to those for ND,

<div class="foldable">
<pre class="Agda">    <a name="20341" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20341" class="Function" target="_blank">f⁺′</a><a name="20344"> </a><a name="20345"     </a><a name="20447" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20341" class="Function" target="_blank">f⁺′</a><a name="20450"> </a><a name="20451" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="20452" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20452" class="Bound" target="_blank">A</a><a name="20453" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="20454"> </a><a name="20455" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="20456" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20456" class="Bound" target="_blank">B</a><a name="20457" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="20458"> </a><a name="20459" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20459" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="20460"> </a><a name="20461" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#89" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">[]</a><a name="20463"> </a><a name="20464" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="20465" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20465" class="Bound" target="_blank">Δ</a><a name="20466" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="20467"> </a><a name="20468" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#20468" class="Bound" target="_blank">f</a><a name="20469">
           </a><a name="20481" class="Comment">-- NJ (Γ ++ A ∷ []) ++ Δ ⊢ .B</a><a name="20510">

It turns out to be very useful to define two helper functions which
introduce and eliminate the empty context to the right. This is
because <span class="Agda Spec"><a class="Bound">Γ</a> <a
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Data.List.Base.html#895"
class="Function Operator" target="_blank">++</a> <a
href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/Agda.Builtin.List.html#89"
class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">[]</a></span> doesn't
automatically reduce. Therefore, any proof in which the empty context
occurs to the right would involve rewriting by <a class="Agda Spec
Function">++&#8209;identityʳ</a>.

### Implicit and Explicit Structural Rules

<pre class="Agda">  <a name="23996" class="Keyword">module</a><a name="24002"> </a><a name="24003" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24003" class="Module" target="_blank">NJ⇔ND</a><a name="24008"> </a><a name="24009" class="Keyword">where</a><a name="24014">

    </a><a name="24020" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24020" class="Function" target="_blank">⟹</a><a name="24021"> </a><a name="24022" class="Symbol">:</a><a name="24023"> </a><a name="24024" class="Symbol">∀</a><a name="24025"> </a><a name="24026" class="Symbol">&#123;</a><a name="24027" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24027" class="Bound" target="_blank">S</a><a name="24028" class="Symbol">&#125;</a><a name="24029"> </a><a name="24030" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="24031"> </a><a name="24032" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#6736" class="Datatype Operator" target="_blank">NJ</a><a name="24034"> </a><a name="24035" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24027" class="Bound" target="_blank">S</a><a name="24036"> </a><a name="24037" class="Symbol">→</a><a name="24038"> </a><a name="24039" href="/2016/one-lambda-calculus-many-times/#5371" class="Datatype Operator">ND</a><a name="24041"> </a><a name="24042" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24027" class="Bound" target="_blank">S</a><a name="24043">

name="24562"> </a><a name="24563" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="24564" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#22093" class="Function" target="_blank">NJ.c⁺′</a><a name="24570"> </a><a name="24571" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24545" class="Bound" target="_blank">Γ</a><a name="24572"> </a><a name="24573" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="24574" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#23749" class="Function" target="_blank">NJ.∅i</a><a name="24579"> </a><a name="24580" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="24581" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#6858" class="InductiveConstructor" target="_blank">⇒e</a><a name="24583"> </a><a name="24584" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="24585" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24446" class="Function" target="_blank">⟸</a><a name="24586"> </a><a name="24587" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24548" class="Bound" target="_blank">f</a><a name="24588" class="Symbol">)</a><a name="24589"> </a><a name="24590" class="Symbol">(</a><a name="24591" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24446" class="Function" target="_blank">⟸</a><a name="24592"> </a><a name="24593" href="https://agda.github.io/agda-stdlib/one-lambda-calculus-many-times-2.html#24550" class="Bound" target="_blank">g</a><a name="24594" class="Symbol">))))</a></pre>


### Sequent Calculus with Explicit Structural Rules

$$
  \begin{array}{c}
  \frac{}{A \vdash A}{\small ax}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash A \quad A , \Delta \vdash B}{\Gamma, \Delta \vdash B}{\small cut}
  \\
  \\
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash A \quad B , \Delta \vdash C}{A \Rightarrow  B , \Gamma, \Delta \vdash C}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!l}
  \quad
  \frac{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\Gamma \vdash A \Rightarrow B}{\small{\Rightarrow}\!r}
  \\
  \\
  \frac{\Gamma \vdash B}{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\small w}
  \quad
  \frac{A , A , \Gamma \vdash B}{A , \Gamma \vdash B}{\small c}
  \quad
  \frac{\Gamma , A , B , \Delta \vdash B}{\Gamma , B , A , \Delta \vdash B}{\small p}
  \end{array}
$$

<pre class="Agda">  <a name="25302" class="Keyword">infix</a><a name="25307"> </a><a name="25308" class="Number">3</a><a name="25309"> LJ_

$$
  \begin{array}{ccccc}
  NJ           & \leftrightarrow & ND           & \rightarrow & Agda \\
  \\
  \updownarrow &                 & \updownarrow &             &      \\
  \\
  LJ           & \leftrightarrow & SC           &             &
  \end{array}
$$

---

[^minproplog]: Or, alternatively, as axiomatisations of minimal
    propositional logic.

[^admit]: As used here, *admit* or *admissible* is a technical term,
    usually contrasted with *derivable*. Derivable rules are rules
    that we can construct directly, without inspecting the
    proofs that we're given as arguments. On the other hand,
    admissible means that we can define these rules, but that we have
    to inspect and rewrite the proofs we're given.
